title="Runtastic">Runtastic</a></li>\n<li>Matix</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.adidas-group.com/">www<wbr />.adidas-group<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Adidas <a href="/wiki/Aktiengesellschaft" title="Aktiengesellschaft">AG</a></b> (<small>German:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[\xcb\x88adi\xcb\x8cdas]</a></span>; stylized as <b>\xc9\x91did\xc9\x91s</b> since 1949) is a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a>, founded and headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Herzogenaurach" title="Herzogenaurach">Herzogenaurach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, that designs and manufactures shoes, clothing and accessories. It is the largest <a href="/wiki/Sportswear_(activewear)" title="Sportswear (activewear)">sportswear</a> manufacturer in Europe, and the second largest in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> for the Adidas Group, which consists of the <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> sportswear company, <a href="/wiki/TaylorMade" title="TaylorMade">TaylorMade</a> golf company (including <a href="/wiki/Ashworth_(clothing)" title="Ashworth (clothing)">Ashworth</a>), <a href="/wiki/Runtastic" title="Runtastic">Runtastic</a>, an Austrian fitness technology company, and 8.33% of <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>, the football club. Adidas\' revenue for 2016 was listed at <a href="/wiki/Euro_sign" title="Euro sign">\xe2\x82\xac</a>19.29 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-AR2016-2_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR2016-2-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company was started by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Dassler" title="Adolf Dassler">Adolf Dassler</a> in his mother\'s house; he was joined by his elder brother <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Dassler" title="Rudolf Dassler">Rudolf</a> in 1924 under the name Dassler Brothers Shoe Factory. Dassler assisted in the development of spiked running shoes (<a href="/wiki/Track_spikes" title="Track spikes">spikes</a>) for multiple athletic events. To enhance the quality of spiked athletic footwear, he transitioned from a previous model of heavy metal spikes to utilising canvas and rubber.  Dassler persuaded U.S. sprinter <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Owens" title="Jesse Owens">Jesse Owens</a> to use his handmade spikes at the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a>. In 1949, following a breakdown in the relationship between the brothers, Adolf created Adidas, and Rudolf established <a href="/wiki/Puma_(brand)" title="Puma (brand)">Puma</a>, which became Adidas\' business rival.<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Adidas\' logo is three stripes, which is used on the company\'s clothing and shoe designs as a marketing aid. The branding, which Adidas bought in 1952 from Finnish sports company <a href="/wiki/Karhu_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Karhu Sports">Karhu Sports</a>, became so successful that Dassler described Adidas as "<a href="/wiki/Three_stripes" title="Three stripes">The three stripes company</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smit_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smit-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The brand name is uncapitalized and is stylized with a lower case "a".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctext">Post-Tapie era</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Products"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Products</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Apparel"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Apparel</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Sportswear"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sportswear</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10"><a href="#Association_football"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Association football</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#Baseball"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12"><a href="#Basketball"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Basketball</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a class="toctext">Golf</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#Gymnastics"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Gymnastics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#Lacrosse"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Lacrosse</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#Running"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.8</span> <span class="toctext">Running</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#Skateboarding"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.9</span> <span class="toctext">Skateboarding</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Tennis"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.10</span> <span class="toctext">Tennis</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Kabaddi"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.11</span> <span class="toctext">Kabaddi</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Accessories"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Accessories</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#Adilette"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Adilette</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23"><a href="#Santiossage"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Santiossage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24"><a href="#Adissage"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Adissage</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Marketing"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Marketing</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Marketing_In_India"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Marketing In India</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Game_advertisement"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Game advertisement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Collaborations"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Collaborations</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Sponsorship"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Sponsorship</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Rivalries"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Rivalries</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Corporate_information"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Corporate information</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Current_executive_board"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Current executive board</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Financial information</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Criticism"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#2011_All_Blacks_replica_rugby_jersey_pricing_controversy"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">2011 All Blacks replica rugby jersey pricing controversy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#2012_&quot;shackle&quot;_sneakers"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">2012 "shackle" sneakers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Sweatshops_and_labour_rights_violations"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sweatshops and labour rights violations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Environmental_record"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Environmental record</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#NCAA_corruption_scandal"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">NCAA corruption scandal</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_days">Early days</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg/170px-Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg/255px-Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg/340px-Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="368" data-file-height="490" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adi.dassler_Skulptur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sculpture of Dassler in the Adi Dassler Stadium, <a href="/wiki/Herzogenaurach" title="Herzogenaurach">Herzogenaurach</a>, Germany</div></div></div>\n<p>Adidas was founded by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Dassler" title="Adolf Dassler">Adolf "Adi" Dassler</a> who made sports shoes in his mother\'s <a href="/wiki/Scullery" title="Scullery">scullery</a> or laundry room in <a href="/wiki/Herzogenaurach" title="Herzogenaurach">Herzogenaurach</a>, Germany after his return from World War I. In July 1924, his older brother Rudolf joined the business, which became Dassler Brothers Shoe Factory (<i lang="de" title="German language text">Gebr\xc3\xbcder Dassler Schuhfabrik</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Sneaker_Wars_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sneaker_Wars-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The electricity supply in Herzogenaurach was unreliable, so the brothers sometimes had to use pedal power from a stationary bicycle to run their equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dassler assisted in the development of <a href="/wiki/Track_spikes" title="Track spikes">spiked running shoes</a> (spikes) for multiple athletic events. To enhance the quality of spiked athletic footwear, he transitioned from a previous model of heavy metal spikes to utilising canvas and rubber.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1936, Dassler persuaded U.S. <a href="/wiki/Sprint_(running)" title="Sprint (running)">sprinter</a> <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Owens" title="Jesse Owens">Jesse Owens</a> to use his hand made spikes at the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a>. Following Owens\' four gold medals, the name and reputation of Dassler shoes became known to the world\'s sportsmen and their trainers. Business was successful and the Dasslers were selling 200,000 pairs of shoes every year before World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-rediff_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rediff-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Dolbury factory, used for production of anti-tank weapons during the Second World War, was nearly destroyed in 1945  by US forces, but was spared when Dassler\'s wife, convinced the GIs that the company and its employees were only interested in manufacturing sports shoes. American occupying forces subsequently became major buyers of the Dassler brothers\' shoes.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Split_and_rivalry_with_Puma">Split and rivalry with Puma</span></h3>\n<p>The brothers split up in 1947 after relations between them had broken down,<sup id="cite_ref-sneakerwars_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sneakerwars-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> with Rudolf forming a new firm that he called <b>Ruda</b> \xe2\x80\x93 from <b>Ru</b>dolf <b>Da</b>ssler, later rebranded <a href="/wiki/Puma_(brand)" title="Puma (brand)">Puma</a>, and Dassler forming a company formally registered as <b>Adidas AG</b> from <b>Adi</b> <b>Das</b>sler on 18 August 1949. Although it is a popular <a href="/wiki/Urban_myth" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban myth">urban myth</a> that the name is an <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a> for <i>All Day I Dream About Sports</i>, that phrase is a "<a href="/wiki/Backronym" title="Backronym">backronym</a>"; the name is a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> formed from "Adi" (a nickname for Adolf) and "Das" (from "Dassler").<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma SE">Puma SE</a> and Adidas entered into a fierce and bitter business rivalry after the split. Indeed, the town of Herzogenaurach was divided on the issue, leading to the nickname "the town of bent necks"\xe2\x80\x94people looked down to see which shoes strangers wore.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Even the town\'s two <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football clubs</a> were divided: <a href="/wiki/ASV_Herzogenaurach" title="ASV Herzogenaurach">ASV Herzogenaurach</a> club was supported by Adidas, while <a href="/wiki/FC_Herzogenaurach" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Herzogenaurach">1 FC Herzogenaurach</a> endorsed Rudolf\'s footwear.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> When handymen were called to Rudolf\'s home, they would deliberately wear Adidas shoes. Rudolf would tell them to go to the basement and pick out a pair of free Pumas.<sup id="cite_ref-DW_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The two brothers were never reconciled and although both are now buried in the same cemetery, they are spaced as far apart as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1948, the first football match after World War II, several members of the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="West Germany national football team">West German national football team</a> wore Puma boots, including the scorer of West Germany\'s first post-war goal, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Burdenski" title="Herbert Burdenski">Herbert Burdenski</a>. Four years later, at the <a href="/wiki/1952_Summer_Olympics" title="1952 Summer Olympics">1952 Summer Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/1500_metres" title="1500 metres">1500 metres</a> runner <a href="/wiki/Josy_Barthel" title="Josy Barthel">Josy Barthel</a> of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> won Puma\'s first Olympic gold in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, Finland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_brand_Adidas.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Logo_brand_Adidas.png/150px-Logo_brand_Adidas.png" width="150" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Logo_brand_Adidas.png/225px-Logo_brand_Adidas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Logo_brand_Adidas.png 2x" data-file-width="284" data-file-height="275" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_brand_Adidas.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The original trefoil Adidas logo until 1998, it is now used on <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Originals" title="Adidas Originals">Adidas Originals</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a>, Puma paid German sprinter <a href="/wiki/Armin_Hary" title="Armin Hary">Armin Hary</a> to wear Pumas in the 100 meter sprint final. Hary had worn Adidas before and asked Adolf for payment, but Adidas rejected this request. The German won gold in Pumas, but then laced up Adidas for the medals ceremony, to the shock of the two Dassler brothers. Hary hoped to cash in from both, but Adi was so enraged he banned the Olympic champion.<sup id="cite_ref-rediff_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rediff-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="3-Stripe_logo">3-Stripe logo</span></h3>\n<p>In 1952, following the <a href="/wiki/1952_Summer_Olympics" title="1952 Summer Olympics">1952 Summer Olympics</a>, Adidas acquired its signature 3-stripe logo from the Finnish athletic footwear brand <a href="/wiki/Karhu_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Karhu Sports">Karhu Sports</a>, for two bottles of whiskey and the equivalent of 1600 euros.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sabotage_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sabotage-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tapie_affair">Tapie affair</span></h3>\n<p>After a period of trouble following the death of Adolf Dassler\'s son <a href="/wiki/Horst_Dassler" title="Horst Dassler">Horst Dassler</a> in 1987, the company was bought in 1989 by French industrialist <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Tapie" title="Bernard Tapie">Bernard Tapie</a>, for <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">\xe2\x82\xa3</a>1.6 <a href="/wiki/1000000000_(number)" class="mw-redirect" title="1000000000 (number)">billion</a> (now \xe2\x82\xac243.9&#160;million), which Tapie borrowed.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Tapie was at the time a famous specialist of rescuing bankrupt companies, an expertise on which he built his fortune.\n</p><p>Tapie decided to move production <a href="/wiki/Offshoring" title="Offshoring">offshore</a> to Asia. He also hired <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> for promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> He sent, from <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a>, New Zealand, a shoe sales representative to Germany and met Adolf Dassler\'s descendants (Amelia Randall Dassler and Bella Beck Dassler) and was sent back with a few items to promote the company there.\n</p><p>In 1992, unable to pay the loan interest, Tapie mandated the <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9dit_Lyonnais" title="Cr\xc3\xa9dit Lyonnais">Cr\xc3\xa9dit Lyonnais</a> bank to sell Adidas,<sup id="cite_ref-Tapie_sale_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tapie_sale-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and the bank subsequently converted the outstanding debt owed into <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">equity</a> of the enterprise, which was unusual as per the prevalent French banking practice. The <a href="/wiki/State-owned" class="mw-redirect" title="State-owned">state-owned</a> bank had tried to get Tapie out of dire financial straits as a personal favour to Tapie, it is reported, because Tapie was <a href="/wiki/Political_minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Political minister">Minister</a> of Urban Affairs (ministre de la Ville) in the French government at the time.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis-Dreyfus" title="Robert Louis-Dreyfus">Robert Louis-Dreyfus</a>, a friend of Bernard Tapie, became the new CEO of the company in 1994. He was also the president of <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Olympique de Marseille</a>, a team Tapie had owned until 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Tapie filed for personal bankruptcy in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-Tapie_sale_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tapie_sale-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He was the object of several lawsuits, notably related to <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">match fixing</a> at the football club. During 1997, he served 6 months of an 18-month prison sentence in <a href="/wiki/La_Sant%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="La Sant\xc3\xa9">La Sant\xc3\xa9</a> prison in Paris. In February 2000, Cr\xc3\xa9dit Lyonnais sold Adidas to Louis-Dreyfus for a much higher amount of money than what Tapie owed, 4.485&#160;billion (\xe2\x82\xac683.514&#160;million) francs rather than 2.85&#160;billion (\xe2\x82\xac434.479&#160;million). They also purposely bankrupted Tapie\'s company that owned Adidas, because only the company had the right to sue them.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Tapie_era">Post-Tapie era</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:An_Adidas_shoe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/An_Adidas_shoe.jpg/200px-An_Adidas_shoe.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/An_Adidas_shoe.jpg/300px-An_Adidas_shoe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/An_Adidas_shoe.jpg/400px-An_Adidas_shoe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:An_Adidas_shoe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Adidas shoe, with the company\'s distinctive <a href="/wiki/Three_stripes" title="Three stripes">three parallel bars</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1994, combined with <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> Youth Group, <a href="/wiki/SOS_Children%27s_Villages" title="SOS Children&#39;s Villages">SOS Children\'s Villages</a> became the main beneficiary.\n</p><p>In 1997, Adidas AG acquired the <a href="/wiki/Salomon_Group" title="Salomon Group">Salomon Group</a> who specialized in ski wear, and its official corporate name was changed to Adidas-Salomon AG. With this acquisition Adidas also acquired the Taylormade Golf company and <a href="/wiki/Maxfli" title="Maxfli">Maxfli</a>, which allowed them to compete with <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> Golf.\n</p><p>In 1998, Adidas sued the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> over their rules limiting the size and number of commercial logos on team uniforms and team clothing. Adidas withdrew the suit, and the two groups established guidelines as to what three-stripe designs would be considered uses of the Adidas trademark.\n</p><p>As CEO of Adidas, Louis-Dreyfus quadrupled revenue to 5.84 billion euros ($7.5 billion) from 1993 through 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, he announced he would resign the following year, due to illness.\n</p><p>In 2003, Adidas filed a lawsuit in a British court challenging Fitness World Trading\'s use of a two-stripe motif similar to Adidas\'s <a href="/wiki/Three_stripes" title="Three stripes">three stripes</a>. The court ruled that despite the simplicity of the mark, <i>Fitness World</i> \'s use was infringing because the public could establish a link between that use and Adidas\'s mark.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2004, top English fashion designer <a href="/wiki/Stella_McCartney" title="Stella McCartney">Stella McCartney</a> launched a joint-venture line with Adidas, establishing a long-term partnership with the corporation. This line is a sports performance collection for women called "Adidas by Stella McCartney",<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and it has been critically acclaimed.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also, on 3 May 2005, Adidas told the public that they sold their partner company <a href="/wiki/Salomon_Group" title="Salomon Group">Salomon Group</a> for \xe2\x82\xac485m to <a href="/wiki/Amer_Sports" title="Amer Sports">Amer Sports</a> of Finland.\nIn August 2005, Adidas declared its intention to buy <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> for $3.8&#160;billion (US$). This takeover was completed with partnership in January 2006<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and meant that the company would have business sales closer to those of Nike in North America. The acquisition of Reebok would also allow Adidas to compete with Nike worldwide as the number two athletic shoemaker in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Adidas has global corporate headquarters in Germany, and many other business locations around the world such as Portland OR, Hong Kong, Toronto, Taiwan, England, Japan, Australia, and Spain.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg/220px-Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg/330px-Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg/440px-Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2632" data-file-height="2234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adidas_Astro_Turfs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adidas has long been a popular manufacturer of astro turf football shoes \xe2\x80\x93 shown here a recent pair that has been a popular choice</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2005, Adidas introduced the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_1" title="Adidas 1">Adidas 1</a>, the first ever production shoe to use a <a href="/wiki/Microprocessor" title="Microprocessor">microprocessor</a>. Dubbed by the company "The World\'s First Intelligent Shoe", it features a microprocessor capable of performing 5 million calculations per second that automatically adjusts the shoe\'s level of cushioning to suit its environment. The shoe requires a small, user-replaceable battery that lasts for approximately 100 hours of running. On 25 November 2005, Adidas released a new version of the Adidas 1 with an increased range of cushioning, allowing the shoe to become softer or firmer, and a new motor with 153 percent more torque.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 April 2006, Adidas announced an 11-year deal to become the official <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> clothing provider. The company has been making <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBDL" class="mw-redirect" title="NBDL">NBDL</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women&#39;s National Basketball Association">WNBA</a> jerseys and products as well as team-coloured versions of the "Superstar" basketball shoe. This deal (worth over $400&#160;million) took over the previous Reebok deal that had been put in place in 2001 for 10 years.\n</p><p>In November 2011, Adidas announced that it would acquire outdoor action sport performance brand Five Ten through a share purchase agreement. The total purchase price was $25 million USD in cash at closing.<sup id="cite_ref-five_ten_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-five_ten-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of 2012, Adidas was reporting their highest revenues ever and Chief Executive Herbert Hainer expressed optimism for the year ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-Dubai_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dubai-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2015, Adidas launched the footwear industry\'s first reservation mobile app. The Adidas Confirmed app allows consumers to get access to and reserve the brand\'s limited edition sneakers by using geo targeting technology<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 March 2015, Adidas and McDonald\'s unveiled the 2015 McDonald\'s All-American uniforms. For the third year in a row, players will be wearing short-sleeved jerseys, made with the same lightweight and breathable material as the ones used in the NBA.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2015, Adidas acquired fitness technology firm <a href="/wiki/Runtastic" title="Runtastic">Runtastic</a> for approximately $240 million.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Apparel">Apparel</span></h3>\n<p>Adidas sells a range of <a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">clothing</a> items, varying from men\'s and women\'s <a href="/wiki/T-shirt" title="T-shirt">t-shirts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacket" title="Jacket">jackets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoodie" title="Hoodie">hoodies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pants" class="mw-redirect" title="Pants">pants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leggings" title="Leggings">leggings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Adidas item of apparel was the <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a> tracksuit created in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Adidas AG is the largest manufacturer of sports bras in Europe, and the second largest manufacturer in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sportswear">Sportswear</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_football">Association football</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG/170px-2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG/255px-2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG/340px-2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="4608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_World_Cup_Autographed_by_the_entire_Spanish_National_Team_that_won_the_2010_World_Cup.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autographed jersey of the <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain national football team</a> that was manufactured by Adidas for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>\n<p>One of the main focuses of Adidas has always been <a href="/wiki/Kit_(association_football)" title="Kit (association football)">football kits</a>, and the associated equipment. Adidas remains a major company in the global supply of team kits for international association football teams and clubs.\n</p><p>Adidas makes <a href="/wiki/Referee_(association_football)" title="Referee (association football)">referee</a> kits that are used in international competition and by many countries and leagues in the world. The company has been an innovator in the area of footwear for the sport, with notable examples including the 1979 release of the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Copa_Mundial" title="Adidas Copa Mundial">Copa Mundial</a> moulded boot used for matches on firm dry pitches. It holds the accolade of the best selling boot of all time. The soft-ground equivalent was named World Cup and it too remains on the market.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DK-Chel15_(8).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/DK-Chel15_%288%29.jpg/170px-DK-Chel15_%288%29.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/DK-Chel15_%288%29.jpg/255px-DK-Chel15_%288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/DK-Chel15_%288%29.jpg/340px-DK-Chel15_%288%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="485" data-file-height="629" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DK-Chel15_(8).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Finale" title="Adidas Finale">Adidas Finale</a>, official match ball of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>, held by playmaker <a href="/wiki/Eden_Hazard" title="Eden Hazard">Eden Hazard</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1970, <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, the world governing body of football, has commissioned <a href="/wiki/List_of_FIFA_World_Cup_official_match_balls" title="List of FIFA World Cup official match balls">specially designed</a> <a href="/wiki/Ball_(association_football)" title="Ball (association football)">footballs</a> for use in its own <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> tournaments. The <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Telstar" title="Adidas Telstar">Adidas Telstar</a> was the first ball commissioned for the World Cup in 1970. The balls supplied for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>, the "<a href="/wiki/Adidas_Teamgeist" title="Adidas Teamgeist">Teamgeist</a>", were particularly noteworthy for their ability to travel further than previous types when struck, leading to longer range goals. Goalkeepers were generally believed to be less comfortable with the design of the ball, claiming it was prone to move significantly and unpredictably in flight.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Adidas introduced the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Jabulani" title="Adidas Jabulani">Jabulani</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a>. The ball was designed and developed by <a href="/wiki/Loughborough_University" title="Loughborough University">Loughborough University</a> in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Brazuca" title="Adidas Brazuca">Adidas Brazuca</a> was the match ball of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 World Cup</a>, the first World Cup ball named by the fans.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg/220px-Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg/330px-Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg/440px-Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2656" data-file-height="1494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adidas_Beau_Jeu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Adidas_Beau_Jeu" title="Adidas Beau Jeu">Adidas Beau Jeu</a>, which translates to <a href="/wiki/The_Beautiful_Game" title="The Beautiful Game">Beautiful Game</a> in English, was an officlal match ball of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Adidas is one of the official sponsors of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Finale" title="Adidas Finale">Adidas Finale</a> is the competition\'s official match ball.<sup id="cite_ref-adidas_Finale_Munich_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adidas_Finale_Munich-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Along with the aforementioned <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Predator" title="Adidas Predator">Adidas Predator</a> boot, Adidas manufactures the <a href="/wiki/AdiPure" title="AdiPure">adiPure</a> range of football boots. Adidas named an official match ball of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> tournament the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Beau_Jeu" title="Adidas Beau Jeu">Adidas Beau Jeu</a> which translates to "<a href="/wiki/The_Beautiful_Game" title="The Beautiful Game">The Beautiful Game</a>" in English.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Adidas provides clothing and equipment for all teams in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span></h4>\n<p>Adidas has also provided baseball equipment and sponsors numerous players of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Professional_Baseball" title="Nippon Professional Baseball">Nippon Professional Baseball</a> in Japan.\n</p><p>Adidas Baseball hardgoods are licensed to Dick\'s Sporting Goods.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1997 to 2008, Adidas sponsored <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span></h4>\n<p>Adidas\' Superstar and Pro Model shoes, affectionately known as "shelltoes" for their stylized hard rubber toe box, were fueled by, among others, coaches such as <a href="/wiki/UCLA" class="mw-redirect" title="UCLA">UCLA</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/John_Wooden" title="John Wooden">John Wooden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>  Adidas drew about even with <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a> in basketball by the mid 1970s before both started to fall behind then-upstart <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, Adidas Superstar became very popular in the 1980s <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_fashion" title="Hip hop fashion">hip hop streetwear</a> scene alongside Adidas\'s stripe-sided polyester suits.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>From 2006 to 2017, Adidas was the outfitter of all 30 franchises in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> brand after Adidas\' acquisition of Reebok. Adidas was replaced by Nike as the official outfitter of the league after the 2016\xe2\x80\x9317 season.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia,_October_2010_(1),_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia%2C_October_2010_%281%29%2C_cropped.jpg/200px-Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia%2C_October_2010_%281%29%2C_cropped.jpg" width="200" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia%2C_October_2010_%281%29%2C_cropped.jpg/300px-Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia%2C_October_2010_%281%29%2C_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia%2C_October_2010_%281%29%2C_cropped.jpg/400px-Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia%2C_October_2010_%281%29%2C_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="463" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tendulkar_batting_against_Australia,_October_2010_(1),_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indian cricketer <a href="/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar" title="Sachin Tendulkar">Sachin Tendulkar</a>, batting with his personalized Adidas Cricket Bat</div></div></div>\n<p>Adidas began manufacturing cricket footwear in the mid 1970s, with their initial target market being Australia. Their shoes were a radical departure from traditional leather cricket boots which had remained basically unchanged for decades, being lighter and more flexible but also offering less toe protection, so that it became not uncommon to see batsmen who had been struck by the ball on the foot hopping around in pain. Having continued to manufacture cricket footwear for many years, in 2006 the company finally entered the field of bat manufacture in 2008 and currently their bat range includes the Pellara, Incurza, Libro and M-Blaster models.\n</p><p>In the 1990s, Adidas signed the superstar Indian batsman <a href="/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar" title="Sachin Tendulkar">Sachin Tendulkar</a> and made shoes for him.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> From 2008 till his retirement, Adidas had sponsored the cricket bat used by Tendulkar. It created a new bat, \'Adidas MasterBlaster Elite\', personalized for him.\n</p><p>In 2008, Adidas made a concerted move into English cricket market by sponsoring English batting star <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Pietersen" title="Kevin Pietersen">Kevin Pietersen</a> after the cancellation of his lifetime deal with Woodworm, when they ran into financial difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The following year they signed up fellow England player <a href="/wiki/Ian_Bell" title="Ian Bell">Ian Bell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistan cricket team">Pakistan</a> opening batsman <a href="/wiki/Salman_Butt" title="Salman Butt">Salman Butt</a> and Indian Player <a href="/wiki/Ravindra_Jadeja" title="Ravindra Jadeja">Ravindra Jadeja</a>.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a> (IPL), Adidas sponsored the team <a href="/wiki/Mumbai_Indians" title="Mumbai Indians">Mumbai Indians</a> from 2008 to 2014 and <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Daredevils" title="Delhi Daredevils">Delhi Daredevils</a> from 2008 to 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> They were the official sponsors of <a href="/wiki/Pune_Warriors_India" title="Pune Warriors India">Pune Warriors India</a> in 2011 and 2012, however the team was banned from IPL due to payment issues. In 2015 Season, Adidas sponsored <a href="/wiki/Royal_Challengers_Bangalore" title="Royal Challengers Bangalore">Royal Challengers Bangalore</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Golf">Golf</span></h4>\n<p><i>Adidas Golf</i> manufactures golf clothing, footwear, and accessories. Men\'s and women\'s equipment includes footwear, shirts, shorts, pants, outerwear (wind suits), base layer and eyewear.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gymnastics">Gymnastics</span></h4>\n<p>From 2000 to 2012, Adidas has provided men\'s and women\'s gymnastics wear for <a href="/wiki/Team_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="Team USA">Team USA</a>, through <a href="/wiki/USA_Gymnastics" title="USA Gymnastics">USA Gymnastics</a>. USA Gymnastics and Adidas sponsorship concluded at the end of 2012. In 2006, Adidas gymnastics leotards for women and Adidas men\'s competition shirts, gymnastics pants and gymnastics shorts have been available in the United States, with seasonal leotards offered for Spring, Summer, Fall and Holidays. Adidas previous collaborated with GK Elite, since Spring 2013, Adidas gymnastics products have been available worldwide through Elegant Sports. USA Olympic team members <a href="/wiki/McKayla_Maroney" title="McKayla Maroney">McKayla Maroney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordyn_Wieber" title="Jordyn Wieber">Jordyn Wieber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jake_Dalton" class="mw-redirect" title="Jake Dalton">Jake Dalton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danell_Leyva" title="Danell Leyva">Danell Leyva</a> are all sponsored by Adidas gymnastics.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lacrosse">Lacrosse</span></h4>\n<p>In 2007, Adidas announced its entering to the <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a> equipment, also sponsoring the Adidas National Lacrosse Classic in July 2008 for the top 600 high school underclassmen players in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The company made their self into their own brand such as "Adidas Lacrosse", getting several scholarships, Bucknell (men and women), Bryant (men), Delaware (men and women), New Jersey Institute of Technology (men), and D3 powerhouse Lynchburg (men and women in fall of 2016 with soft good only)". Materials that adidas provided were jerseys, shorts, shoes, shafts, heads, gloves, and protective pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Products manufactured for the sport are <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse_stick" title="Lacrosse stick">sticks</a>, gloves, protective gear and boots.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Running">Running</span></h4>\n<p>Adidas currently manufactures several running and lifestyle shoes, including the Energy-boost, and the spring-blade trainers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (October 2012)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>I The brand has built a strong runners\' network within big European capitals, such as Paris\' "Boost Energy League". In 2016 the 3rd season launched. In Paris, the Boost Energy League gathers 11 teams representing different districts of Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Adidas launched two new color ways of the NMD R1 and one new color way of the NMD XR1 in September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\nadidas EQT is a style of sneakers from adidas. It originated in the early 90s and relaunched in 2017. The latest adidas EQT line released in a \xe2\x80\x9cTuro Red\xe2\x80\x9d Pack on January 26, 2017, and included models such as the adidas EQT Support 93/17, EQT Support ADV, and EQT Support Ultra. adidas.com is one of the few online retailers.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg/220px-Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg/330px-Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg/440px-Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4128" data-file-height="2322" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adidas_Running_Shoe_Demo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adidas running shoe demo in Boston</div></div></div>\n<p>In November 2016, Adidas teased a sneaker made from ocean plastic. The shoe is created from a fabric called "<a href="/wiki/BioSteel" title="BioSteel">Biosteel</a>". The shoe is called the "Adidas Futurecraft Biofabric." The material used is 15% lighter than conventional silk fibers, and is 100% biodegradable. The shoe only begin to dissolve when it is put in contact with a high concentration of the digestion enzyme proteinase, which occurs naturally. Once this happens, the shoes can decompose within 36 hours. The shoe was never released.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Skateboarding">Skateboarding</span></h4>\n<p>Adidas Skateboarding produces shoes made specifically for skateboarding, including the redesign of previous models for skateboarding. The brand also releases signature models designed by team riders.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tennis">Tennis</span></h4>\n<p>Adidas has been involved with tennis equipment since the mid 1960s and has historically sponsored many top tennis players, beginning with two of the most dominant male tennis players at the start of the professional era in the late 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Smith" title="Stan Smith">Stan Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ilie_Nastase" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilie Nastase">Ilie Nastase</a>. During the 1980s and 1990s, not only were they exclusive apparel and footwear sponsors of world number one men\'s tennis players <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Lendl" title="Ivan Lendl">Ivan Lendl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Edberg" title="Stefan Edberg">Stefan Edberg</a> and ladies\' world number one <a href="/wiki/Steffi_Graf" title="Steffi Graf">Steffi Graf</a> but each player had their own, exclusive graphic styles designed for their use during play, which were in turn marketed to the general public. Ivan Lendl even spent the vast majority of his dominant career playing with several different models of Adidas tennis racquets, primarily using the legendary Adidas GTX-Pro and then later the Adidas GTX Pro-T. The company recently introduced a new line of tennis <a href="/wiki/Racquet" class="mw-redirect" title="Racquet">racquets</a>. While the Feather is made for the "regular player", and the Response for the "club player", Adidas targets the "tournament player" with the 12.2 oz Barricade tour model.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kabaddi">Kabaddi</span></h4>\n<p>Adidas entered <a href="/wiki/Kabaddi" title="Kabaddi">Kabaddi</a> which is still a non-Olympic sport but highly popular in the Indian subcontinent and Asian countries. In 2014, with the launch of <a href="/wiki/Pro_Kabaddi_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro Kabaddi League">Pro Kabaddi League</a> a city based franchise league in India, kabaddi took the region with storm. In 2015, they tied up with Mumbai-based franchise <a href="/wiki/U_Mumba" title="U Mumba">U Mumba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>"The association of kabaddi with adidas is a clear exemplification of the growth of the sport over the last two years," shared U Sports CEO, Supratik Sen.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accessories">Accessories</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FreshImpactLimited.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/FreshImpactLimited.JPG/150px-FreshImpactLimited.JPG" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/FreshImpactLimited.JPG/225px-FreshImpactLimited.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/FreshImpactLimited.JPG/300px-FreshImpactLimited.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3189" data-file-height="4800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FreshImpactLimited.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adidas "Fresh Impact" - Limited Edition bottle</div></div></div>\n<p>Adidas also designs and makes <a href="/wiki/Slide_(footwear)" title="Slide (footwear)">slide</a>-style sandals, mobile accessories,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> watches, <a href="/wiki/Glasses" title="Glasses">eyewear</a>, bags, <a href="/wiki/Baseball_cap" title="Baseball cap">baseball caps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sock" title="Sock">socks</a>. As well, Adidas has a branded range of male and female <a href="/wiki/Deodorant" title="Deodorant">deodorants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perfume" title="Perfume">perfumes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aftershave" title="Aftershave">aftershave</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lotion" title="Lotion">lotions</a>.\n</p><p>Adidas announced they would be launching a new $199 Fit Smart wristband in mid-August 2014. The wristband will pair with Adidas\'s miCoach app, which acts as a personal trainer.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adilette">Adilette</span></h4>\n<p>Adilette was the first ever pair of <a href="/wiki/Sandals" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandals">sandals</a> made by Adidas, originally developed in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Adidas claims that a group of athletes approached <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Dassler" title="Adolf Dassler">Adi Dassler</a> requesting a shoe be made for the locker room.\n</p><p>To this day, the resulting sandals are a best-seller.<sup id="cite_ref-history-60_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-60-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Since the original navy blue and white <b>Adilette</b> sandals were created nearly fifty years ago, more varieties have been created in different colours (black, red, green, grey, orange, brown, yellow, pink, golden, silver). Most recently, Adidas has introduced a colour scheme that goes along with its Predator and adizero line; the scheme is dubbed warning (orange) and purple. Usually, the three stripes appear in the contrasting colour on the strap of the classic models. The most common adilette livery is in navy blue or black, mixed with white colours. Also the Woodilette and Trefoil models follow a similar design but without stripes on the strap.\n</p><p>The model provides a contoured orthopedic rubber sole with synthetic upper, and was designed as an apr\xc3\xa8s-sport <a href="/wiki/Slide_(footwear)" title="Slide (footwear)">slide</a>, but the adilette were quickly used everywhere out of the sporting world. Opting for a wide, over the foot strap rather than the design of <a href="/wiki/Flip_flops" class="mw-redirect" title="Flip flops">flip flops</a>, the adilette sandals provide a fresh style and a different level of comfort for the wearer. The strap is also glued to the sides of the sandal, which directs tension to less stressful areas of the sandal, which gives the sandals more durability.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Santiossage">Santiossage</span></h4>\n<p>The <b>Santiossage</b> is a uni-sex <a href="/wiki/Slide_(footwear)" title="Slide (footwear)">slide</a>-style sandal. The sandal has the trademarked three stripes on a velcro strap toward the front of the shoe. <a href="/wiki/Santiossage" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiossage">Santiossage</a> comes in black, navy, or red. On the side of the shoe, toward the heel on either side, the manufacturer\'s name appears, as well as on a round emblem in the actual heel of the foot-bed. Notably, there are tiny clear massage nubs throughout the foot-bed for the purpose of massaging after-sport footaches, although the sandals are worn casually among non-athletes. Seen through these clear nubs are Adidas\' three stripes.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adissage">Adissage</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adissage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Adissage.jpg/200px-Adissage.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Adissage.jpg/300px-Adissage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Adissage.jpg/400px-Adissage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adissage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pair of Adissage</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Adissage</b> is also a uni-sex <a href="/wiki/Slide_(footwear)" title="Slide (footwear)">slide</a>-style sandal. Available in black, navy, light blue, black with pink, and other assorted colors, the sandal has the trademarked three stripes on a <a href="/wiki/Velcro" title="Velcro">velcro</a> strap toward the front of the shoe. On the side of the shoe, toward the heel on either side, the manufacturers name appears, as well as on a round emblem in the actual heel of the footbed. Like the <b>Santiossage</b>, there are tiny black massage nubs throughout the foot-bed for the purpose of massaging foot aches after sport, although popular as a casual sandal amongst non-athletes as well.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg/150px-Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg" width="150" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg/225px-Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg/300px-Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1138" data-file-height="2145" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilbao_BUM_Chuck_D_chandal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chuck_D" title="Chuck D">Chuck D</a> in an Adidas sweatsuit</div></div></div>\n<p>Adidas, like other sports brands, is believed to engender high consumer brand loyalty. Brand loyalty towards Adidas, <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike, Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puma_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma AG">Puma AG</a> and several other sportswear brands was examined in a recent study.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The study found consumers did not exhibit unduly high loyalty towards such brands.\n</p><p>During the mid to late 1990s, Adidas divided the brand into three main groups with each a separate focus: <b>Adidas Performance</b> was designed to maintain their devotion to the athlete; <b><a href="/wiki/Adidas_Originals" title="Adidas Originals">Adidas Originals</a></b> was designed to focus on the brand\'s earlier designs which remained a popular life-style icon; and <b>Style Essentials</b>, which dealt with the fashion market; the main group within this being <b>Y-3</b> (which is a collaboration between Adidas and renowned Japanese fashion designer <a href="/wiki/Yohji_Yamamoto" title="Yohji Yamamoto">Yohji Yamamoto</a> - the Y representing Yamamoto and the 3 representing the three stripes of Adidas).\n</p><p>Launched in 2004, <i>"Impossible is Nothing"</i> is one of the company\'s most memorable campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The campaign was developed by 180/TBWA based in Amsterdam, but significant work was also done by <a href="/wiki/TBWA%5CChiat%5CDay" title="TBWA\\Chiat\\Day">TBWA\\Chiat\\Day</a> in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-new_brand_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_brand-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> A few years later, Adidas launched a basketball specific campaign -- "<i>Believe in 5ive</i>"\xe2\x80\x94for the 2006-2007 NBA season.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, <i>"Adidas is all in"</i> became the global marketing strategy slogan for Adidas. The slogan aimed to tie all brands and labels together, presenting a unified image to consumers interested in sports, fashion, street, music and pop culture. There appears to be connection with the phrase "all-in" meaning "exhausted" in some English speaking nations.\n</p><p>In 2015, Adidas launched "<i>Creating the New</i>" as its new strategic business plan until 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> This plan has three strategic choices: speed, cities and open source.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_In_India">Marketing In India</span></h3>\n<p>India has been a very speculative market for Adidas. Despite this Dave Thomas, managing director of Adidas in India is ambitious of the country\'s potential.<sup id="cite_ref-Why_Adidas_is_cool_again_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Adidas_is_cool_again-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The company hopes to double its revenue from Rs. 805 crores by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Why_Adidas_is_cool_again_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Adidas_is_cool_again-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, the company had signed <a href="/wiki/Ranveer_Singh" title="Ranveer Singh">Ranveer Singh</a> a prominent Bollywood actor as a brand ambassador to the company\'s products.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ranveer_Singh" title="Ranveer Singh">Ranveer</a> then was a budding actor. The company later decided to use the people\'s almost religious adoration for the game cricket to promote their brand. It soon launched a new cricket campaign in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The campaign was called FeelLoveUseHate with prominent Indian cricketer Virat Kohli.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> However, in 2017, Virat Kohli was removed as the brand ambassador of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The cricketer later signed a major deal with Puma India.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The company also sells its products online through e-commerce websites such as Myntra, Snapdeal, Jabong and Amazon. Adidas also has a website dedicated to the Indian audience that markets and sells products to its consumers in India.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_advertisement">Game advertisement</span></h3>\n<p>The brand is featured in several games, including <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Commodore Amiga</a>: <i>Daley Thompson\'s Olympic Challenge</i>, <a href="/wiki/Sony_PlayStation" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony PlayStation">Sony PlayStation</a>: <i>Adidas power soccer</i> and Commodore 64, ZX spectrum, Amstrad CPC: <i><a href="/wiki/Adidas_Championship_Football" title="Adidas Championship Football">Adidas Championship Football</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborations">Collaborations</span></h3>\n<p>Adidas has done several collaborations with well known designers, including <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Scott" title="Jeremy Scott">Jeremy Scott</a>, Alexander Wang, and Raf Simons. They have also reached out to several celebrities, such as Kanye West, Pharrell Williams, and Stan Smith to create some of the company\'s most notable and coveted pieces.\n</p><p>On 14 February 2015, Kanye West collaborated with Adidas to create the first pair of Yeezys, eventually leading to his own clothing line which would transform the lifestyle and streetwear industry.<sup id="cite_ref-newcontract_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newcontract-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span></h2>\n<div sponsor <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Other clubs include <a
